<p><b>Brisbane Roar Football Club</b> is a professional Australian <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> It competes in the country's premier competition, the <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>, under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_professional_sports_league_organization#Systems_around_the_world" title="North American professional sports league organization">licence</a> from <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia" title="Football Federation Australia">Football Federation Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A-League_Licence_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-A-League_Licence-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club was formed in 1958 as Hollandia-Inala, and became Brisbane Lions, before it transitioned into Queensland Roar, playing under that name from the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_A-League" title="2005–06 A-League">2005–06 season</a> of the A-League until the 2008–09 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Since joining the A-League, the club has won two league Premierships, three Championships and it has competed in two <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> competitions. Brisbane Roar holds the record for the longest unbeaten run at the top level of any Australian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_code" title="Football code">football code</a>, which stands at 36 league matches without defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-footballaustralia.com.au_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-footballaustralia.com.au-4">[4]</a></sup> Brisbane Roar are also the first and only club to win back to back A-League Championships.</p>
<p>The club plays matches at <a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Suncorp Stadium</a>, a 52,500 seat multi-use venue in <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Queensland" title="Milton, Queensland">Milton</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Ballymore_Stadium" title="Ballymore Stadium">Ballymore Stadium</a> serving as the club's training base from 2016 onwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Roar_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Roar-5">[5]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar_FC_Youth" title="Brisbane Roar FC Youth">youth team</a> competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Youth_League_(Australia)" title="National Youth League (Australia)">National Youth League</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar_FC_(W-League)" title="Brisbane Roar FC (W-League)">women's team</a> competes in the <a href="/wiki/W-League_(Australia)" title="W-League (Australia)">W-League</a>. As of 2014, the youth and women's teams also compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Premier_Leagues_Queensland" title="National Premier Leagues Queensland">NPL Queensland</a> in order to maintain fitness and further develop their abilities. The youth team competes in the senior men's division while the women's team compete in the U15 boy's division. The youth and women matches are played at various locations across Brisbane, including <a href="/wiki/Goodwin_Park" title="Goodwin Park">Goodwin Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Sport_and_Athletics_Centre" title="Queensland Sport and Athletics Centre">QSAC</a>, <a href="/wiki/A.J._Kelly_Park" title="A.J. Kelly Park">A.J. Kelly Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perry_Park,_Brisbane" title="Perry Park, Brisbane">Perry Park</a> and occasionally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suncorp_Stadium" title="Suncorp Stadium">Suncorp Stadium</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_formation_.281957.E2.80.932004.29">Origins and formation (1957–2004)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins and formation (1957–2004)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Lions_FC" title="Queensland Lions FC">Queensland Lions FC</a></div>
<p>The origins of Brisbane Roar are traced back to the founding of Hollandia-Inala in 1957, by Dutch immigrants. The club was based in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane,_Queensland" title="Brisbane, Queensland">Brisbane</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Richlands,_Queensland" title="Richlands, Queensland">Richlands</a>. After adopting the name Brisbane Lions in the 1970s, the club joined the <a href="/wiki/National_Soccer_League" title="National Soccer League">National Soccer League</a> (NSL) as one of the founding clubs in the <a href="/wiki/1977_National_Soccer_League" title="1977 National Soccer League">1977 season</a> and competed until the end of the <a href="/wiki/1988_National_Soccer_League" title="1988 National Soccer League">1988 season</a> before reverting down to the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Premier_League" title="Brisbane Premier League">Brisbane Premier League</a> thereafter. In the 1990s, the club again changed its name to <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Lions_FC" title="Queensland Lions FC">Queensland Lions</a> after coming to an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> club, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Lions" title="Brisbane Lions">Brisbane Lions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aap_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-aap-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the time of conception of the <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>, teams from several capital cities were preferred to form the foundation clubs. By June 2004, two of the twenty submissions for joining the league were sought by partnerships formed in Brisbane, the capital of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queensland,_Australia" title="Queensland, Australia">Queensland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> On 1 November 2004, the group headed by Queensland Lions were chosen as operators of the Brisbane team. On 2 March the following year, Queensland Roar FC were officially announced. The clubs's first-ever board consisted of chairman <a href="/wiki/John_Ribot" title="John Ribot">John Ribot</a>, a former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Executive" title="Chief Executive">CEO</a> of both <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> clubs <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Broncos" title="Brisbane Broncos">Brisbane Broncos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Storm" title="Melbourne Storm">Melbourne Storm</a>, deputy chairman Gary Wilkins, former Queensland and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australia_national_association_football_team" title="Australia national association football team">Australian</a> international player, and CEO Lawrence Oudendyk, who was also Queensland Lions CEO.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_.282004.E2.80.932009.29">Early years (2004–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years (2004–2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="427" data-file-width="754" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg/220px-Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg/330px-Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg/440px-Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qld_roar_suncorp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Roar playing at home in 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Miron_Bleiberg" title="Miron Bleiberg">Miron Bleiberg</a> was appointed as the then Queensland Roar's inaugural manager on 2 March 2005. Under pressure from the fans to deliver on his promises of attractive, attacking and successful football he resigned on 12 November 2006 following a poor start to the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_A-League" title="2006–07 A-League">2006–07</a> season. After much speculation, Bleiberg was replaced by former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australia_national_association_football_team" title="Australia national association football team">Australian</a> national team coach, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Farina" title="Frank Farina">Frank Farina</a> just three days after Bleiberg's resignation.</p>
<p>Frank Farina's arrival led to a mini-revival which saw the club narrowly miss out on what would have been the Roar's first finals appearance, on goal difference. The <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_A-League" title="2007–08 A-League">2007–08</a> season, however, saw Farina make up for the shortfall of the previous season, qualifying for the finals for the first time in the club's history. A memorable performance in the second leg of the semi-final saw the Roar defeat arch rivals 2–0 (2–0 agg.) <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a> in front of a (then) club record 36,221 fans to qualify for the preliminary final against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newcastle_Jets" title="Newcastle Jets">Newcastle Jets</a>. The Roar would controversially lose 3–2 to the Newcastle side, who would ultimately go on to win the Grand Final. Farina again qualified for the finals in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_A-League" title="2008–09 A-League">2008–09</a>, where the Roar dispatched of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Coast_Mariners" title="Central Coast Mariners">Central Coast Mariners</a> 4–2 on aggregate, however they ultimately lost, again in the preliminary final, to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adelaide_United" title="Adelaide United">Adelaide United</a> after failing to capitalise on their dominance.</p>
<p>In 2009, the club was officially renamed to Brisbane Roar Football Club due to two other Queensland-based clubs entering the competition; that being <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_United_FC" title="Gold Coast United FC">Gold Coast United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Fury_FC" title="Northern Fury FC">North Queensland Fury</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brisbane_Times_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brisbane_Times-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 October 2009, Farina was arrested by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queensland_Police" title="Queensland Police">Queensland Police</a> for <a href="/wiki/Driving_under_the_influence" title="Driving under the influence">Driving under the influence</a>. He was initially suspended by the Roar and asked to show cause as to why he should not be sacked for tarnishing the name of the club. It was announced that assistant manager, Rado Vidošić would step into a caretakers role until a decision had been made which would include the M1 Derby, which the Roar lost 1–0 at home. Farina was ultimately sacked on 14 October 2009, with the club tasked with finding a replacement for the femainder of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Brisbane_Roar_FC_season" title="2009–10 Brisbane Roar FC season">2009–10 season</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postecoglou_era_.282009.E2.80.932012.29">Postecoglou era (2009–2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Postecoglou era (2009–2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Besart_Berisha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1447" data-file-width="2048" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Besart_Berisha.jpg/220px-Besart_Berisha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Besart_Berisha.jpg/330px-Besart_Berisha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Besart_Berisha.jpg/440px-Besart_Berisha.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Besart_Berisha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Besart_Berisha" title="Besart Berisha">Besart Berisha</a>, became the clubs top-scorer.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ange_Postecoglou" title="Ange Postecoglou">Ange Postecoglou</a> arrived mid-season armed with the task of picking up the pieces of a season in tatters. Postecoglou's first season ended as the worst in the club's short history, finishing second from the bottom. Postecoglou completed a turn-around in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_A-League" title="2010–11 A-League">2010–11</a> season. He made wholesale changes to the squad, commencing with the replacement of the "old-guard" of <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Miller" title="Charlie Miller">Charlie Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Moore" title="Craig Moore">Craig Moore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Tiatto" title="Danny Tiatto">Danny Tiatto</a> and brought in his own squad which was a mixture of youth and talented experience. Under his brand of possession/attacking football, he would lead the team to win the club's inaugural premiership and go on to complete the club's first <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">Double</a> by also wrapping up the championship in a memorable <a href="/wiki/2011_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2011 A-League Grand Final">2011 A-League Grand Final</a> in front of a then club record 50,168 supporters. The club went on an Australian sporting record 36-match unbeaten run which commenced in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_A-League" title="2010–11 A-League">2010–11</a> season and ran through to the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_A-League" title="2011–12 A-League">2011–12</a> season. After much speculation on his future at the club, it was reported that Postecoglou had signed a three-year contract extension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-couriermail.com.au_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-couriermail.com.au-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>With such a successful season behind him, there was much talk as to whether the Roar could equal or better that in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_A-League" title="2011–12 A-League">2011–12</a> season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Their title credentials were in doubt when the club went on a club-record worst losing streak of five matches immediately following the ending of their record 36-match unbeaten streak. Postecoglou remained steadfast in the club's footballing philosophy and the club went on to record just one loss in the last 14 games of the regular season to finish league runners-up. Unable to retain the Premiers Plate, Postecoglou led the club to back-to-back championships in the <a href="/wiki/2012_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2012 A-League Grand Final">2012 A-League Grand Final</a> in front of a club-record 50,344 supporters. Postecoglou also led the Roar's initial foray into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Asian_Champions_League" title="2012 Asian Champions League">2012 Asian Champions League</a> as reward for their success in the previous season. Success was mixed, picking up two draws from four matches.</p>
<p>On 24 April 2012, Postecoglou left the club by way of mutual consent, citing a desire to seek "a new challenge".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Ange leaves the club as the most successful manager in the club's history.</p>
<p>On 26 April 2012, it was reported that Postecoglou did not, in fact, sign a new contract at the conclusion of the 2010–11 season due to the uncertainty around the club's ownership at the time. That allowed his original two-year contract with the club to expire at the conclusion of the 2011–12 season and leave to join <span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Melbourne Victory !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Victory_FC" title="Melbourne Victory FC">Melbourne Victory</a></span> without the Victory needing to pay out his "contract" with the Roar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_success_.282012.E2.80.93present.29">Recent success (2012–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent success (2012–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 April 2012, <a href="/wiki/Rado_Vido%C5%A1i%C4%87" title="Rado Vidošić">Rado Vidošić</a> was promoted to the managers' position after serving seven years as Assistant Manager under the three previous managers before him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> On 18 December 2012, Vidošić was removed as coach, taking up the role of technical director for the club, with <a href="/wiki/Mike_Mulvey" title="Mike Mulvey">Mike Mulvey</a>, then coach of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melbourne_Victory_FC_W-League" title="Melbourne Victory FC W-League">Melbourne Victory women's</a> named as his replacement. Vidošić was only manager for 13 matches before transferring to the new role, similar to the one offered to Postecoglou before his exit earlier in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-restructure_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-restructure-14">[14]</a></sup> At the end of the 2012–13 season, the Roar finished in 5th place, carried by striker <a href="/wiki/Besart_Berisha" title="Besart Berisha">Besart Berisha</a>'s 14 goals during the season. The club made it to the semi-finals in the finals series, bowing out to premiers <a href="/wiki/Western_Sydney_Wanderers_FC" title="Western Sydney Wanderers FC">Western Sydney Wanderers</a> 2–0.</p>
<p>The 2013/14 season began in terrific style, with the Roar winning 8 of their first 10 games. This form continued for the rest of the season as the club became dominant premiers. Players like <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Franjic" title="Ivan Franjic">Ivan Franjic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luke_Brattan" title="Luke Brattan">Luke Brattan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dimitri_Petratos" title="Dimitri Petratos">Dimitri Petratos</a> shone while the return of former captain <a href="/wiki/Matt_McKay" title="Matt McKay">Matt McKay</a> bolstered the midfield. Brisbane won the grand final 2–1 after extra time against Western Sydney Wanderers. Club talisman Besart Berisha and star utility Ivan Franjic would leave the club over the off-season for Melbourne Victory and <a href="/wiki/FC_Torpedo_Moscow" title="FC Torpedo Moscow">Torpedo Moscow</a> respectively.</p>
<p>After a run of poor results at the beginning of the 2014–15 season, Mulvey stepped down from the head coach role. <a href="/wiki/Frans_Thijssen" title="Frans Thijssen">Frans Thijssen</a> was appointed caretaker coach for the remainder of the season. Captain Matt Smith left the club in December to join <a href="/wiki/Bangkok_Glass_F.C." title="Bangkok Glass F.C.">Bangkok Glass</a>, and was replaced by former captain and club favourite Matt McKay. The season ended with the club recovering to finish in 6th position and qualify for the finals series. Brisbane were knocked out by Adelaide United in the elimination final 2–1.</p>
<p>On 26 May 2015, <a href="/wiki/John_Aloisi" title="John Aloisi">John Aloisi</a> was appointed head coach. Amidst off-field drama regarding the club's ownserhip during his first season as head coach, Aloisi led the Roar to an encouraging 3rd place on the ladder, narrowly missing out on the championship.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crest_and_colours">Crest and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Crest and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_roar.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="175" data-file-width="291" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Brisbane_roar.svg/200px-Brisbane_roar.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Brisbane_roar.svg/300px-Brisbane_roar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Brisbane_roar.svg/400px-Brisbane_roar.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">Roar's first kit</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the first two seasons the Roar played in a predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orange_(color)" title="Orange (color)">orange</a> home strip with blue shorts and maroon socks. <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> sporting teams traditionally play in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maroon_(color)" title="Maroon (color)">maroon</a> but the original home strip kept with the colours used by the team in its earlier incarnations. The colours of orange and blue honour the club's <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> origins. On 31 July 2007 the club announced that it had ordered a strip that was half orange and half maroon, but that the colours were manufactured for prominence on television. For season three the home kit had been redesigned, the home strip is still orange but features maroon sleeves, the shorts are maroon instead of blue and orange socks are worn. <a href="/wiki/Danny_Tiatto" title="Danny Tiatto">Danny Tiatto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Moore" title="Craig Moore">Craig Moore</a> modelled in the strip launch on 1 August 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_A-League" title="2009–10 A-League">2009–10 A-League season</a>, in accordance with the name changing of the club from Queensland Roar to Brisbane Roar, the club's logo was also changed with "Queensland" being dropped to make way for "Brisbane". On 20 May 2009, <a href="/wiki/Reinaldo_Elias_da_Costa" title="Reinaldo Elias da Costa">Reinaldo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergio_van_Dijk" title="Sergio van Dijk">Sergio van Dijk</a> unveiled a new kit for the club, which would be worn for the next two seasons. The club stuck with the maroon and orange they had used for the last kit, but instead opted to drop the white slashes on the home kit. The orange used for the previous kit was brightened to the one used in season 1 of the <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>, with the design of both the new home and away kits changing. The slashes were dropped for a shoulder-pad style. The maroon shoulder pads would be displayed on an orange body, with maroon shorts. This was reversed on the away kit, with the shoulder-pads being orange on a white body with orange shorts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_A-League" title="2011–12 A-League">2011–12 A-League season</a>, the club announced that maroon, which had featured in some way on the clubs' kits since the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_A-League" title="2005–06 A-League">A-League inception</a>, would be removed and replaced with black.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> On 5 September 2011, the club released their kits for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Brisbane_Roar_season" title="2011–12 Brisbane Roar season">upcoming season</a>. The club showed off their home kit, which was orange with black diagonal shoulders with a thin, white line under the black. This was supported by orange with black banded socks. The away kit would turn out to be predominately black, with only the orange shoulders on the top with the white line underneath and the black with orange banded socks. The same pants would be used for both the home and away kits, which would sport two orange bands and a white band on black pants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The kits released were almost identical to the same design used by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_FC" title="Tottenham Hotspur FC">Tottenham Hotspur</a> during their <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2010–11 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2010–11 season</a> with the only difference being full diagonal sashes and a collared neck instead of a "V" neck.</p>
<p>After two seasons in the diagonally sashed kit, both yielding <a href="/wiki/A-League#Finals_series" title="A-League">Final Series</a> football, the first season, winning the <a href="/wiki/2012_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2012 A-League Grand Final">Grand Final</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" title="Puma SE">Puma</a> released a new set of kits, including, for the first time, an alternative strip, deemed by the club as an "Event" kit. The home kit consisted of the usual orange, with black sides, black arm cuffs and a black V-neck collar, which also had a white piece of round-collared fabric attached, which had 3 centrally based lines, white in the centre, orange on the left and black on the right with white on the outside of the black and orange lines. The away kit reverted to the white with orange sides, black arm cuffs and a black V-neck collar. As with the home kit, the away kit had an orange piece of collared fabric attached to the collar, which had 3 centrally based lines, orange in the middle with a white stripe on the left and black on the right of the orange stripe with orange on the outside of the black and white lines. The alternative, or "event" strip, was silver with a top left to bottom right, orange diagonal sash. It also had black arm cuffs and a black V-neck collar with the inner silver fabric and the 3 centrally based stripes. Silver stripe in the middle with a black stripe on either side of the silver stripe and silver on the outside of the two black stripes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 August 2014, before the <a href="/wiki/2014_FFA_Cup#Round_of_32" title="2014 FFA Cup">2014 FFA Cup</a> game vs <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Lions_SC" title="Stirling Lions SC">Stirling Lions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Brisbane_Roar_FC_season" title="2014–15 Brisbane Roar FC season">2014–15 season</a>,the Roar would reveal that <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a> would be making their kits for the next 4 years, ending a 4-year tenure with <a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" title="Puma SE">Puma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_crest_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_crest-20">[20]</a></sup> Two days later, Brisbane Roar changed their logo to a more "traditional" shield type crest, the biggest change since the club was renamed ahead of the 2009–10 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_crest_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_crest-20">[20]</a></sup> The revelation received mixed reviews, some saying it lost the plastic, American franchise logo feel and some saying it's too bland and that not enough time was put into it. Another 2 days later, the Roar would release their new Umbro home kit, ditching the black pants and going with an all orange kit. The top would be completely orange with white piping on the collar with the pants being orange as well and have a white vertical strip going 3/4 of the way up the sides of the pants from the bottom, topped off with orange socks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsors">Sponsors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sponsors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>On 30 November 2007, the club signed a two and a half year deal with cafe chain <a href="/wiki/The_Coffee_Club" title="The Coffee Club">The Coffee Club</a> to be their main shirt sponsor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Coffee Club would re-sign with the Roar in August 2010 for another 3 years, making it one of the longest sponsorship deals in the <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> After the club's licence was taken back by <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia" title="Football Federation Australia">Football Federation Australia</a> in March 2011, the Coffee Club committed their future to the club, signing a $2 Million dollar, 3-year contract extension, sealing their future as sponsors until at least 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-couriermail.com.au_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-couriermail.com.au-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the conclusion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010-11_A-League" title="2010-11 A-League">2010-11 A-League</a> season, the League's collective kit deal with <a href="/wiki/Reebok" title="Reebok">Reebok</a> came to an end meaning that all A-League clubs could enter into their own separate kit manufacturer agreements. On 2 August 2011, the Roar announced that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puma_AG" title="Puma AG">Puma</a> would be the clubs' first kit manufacturer decided by the club, and agreed to a three-year deal with the sports brand. The club announced that Puma will manufacture the official playing kits for all Brisbane Roar teams, including the Youth and Women’s teams as well as replica kits and other merchandise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PUMA_partner_with_Brisbane_Roar_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-PUMA_partner_with_Brisbane_Roar-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the start of the 2014/15 A-League season Brisbane Roar announced that Umbro would be replacing Puma as the clubs playing kit and apparel partner for the next four seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> On 24 February 2015, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Griffith_University" title="Griffith University">Griffith University</a> would be the principal kit Sponsor for the <a href="/wiki/2015_AFC_Champions_League" title="2015 AFC Champions League">2015 AFC Champions League</a> campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Griffith_University_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Griffith_University-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 July 2015, it was announced that former front shirt sponsor, <a href="/wiki/The_Coffee_Club" title="The Coffee Club">The Coffee Club</a> will not renew its sponsorship with the club for the 2015/16 season. It was then announced that Ladbrokes will be the front shirt sponsor for the Roar's friendly against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> on 17 July 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Steadfast were announced as "Principal Partners" and "Front of Shirt Sponsors" by the club on 10 August 2015 for the duration of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015-16_A-League" title="2015-16 A-League">2015-16 A-League</a> season. Steadfast had previously sponsored the rear of the men's teams' shirts and this new partnership will see the Steadfast logo feature on the shirts of all three Brisbane Roar teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium_and_facilities">Stadium and facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Stadium and facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="790" data-file-width="1205" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg/220px-Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg/330px-Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg/440px-Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Suncorp-Stadium-Milton-Queensland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brisbane Roar play home matches at <a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Lang Park</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since their inception, Brisbane Roar have played their home matches at the 52,500-capacity <a href="/wiki/Lang_Park" title="Lang Park">Lang Park</a> (known as Suncorp Stadium for sponsorship reasons) in the inner-city suburb of <a href="/wiki/Milton,_Queensland" title="Milton, Queensland">Milton</a>. The stadium was also the home ground for the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Strikers_FC" title="Brisbane Strikers FC">Brisbane Strikers</a> in the now-defunct <a href="/wiki/National_Soccer_League" title="National Soccer League">NSL</a>. The stadium was also one of five venues in the successful <a href="/wiki/1993_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1993 FIFA World Youth Championship">1993 FIFA World Youth Championship</a> where the ground hosted seven matches. Suncorp Stadium has hosted Australian international fixtures, games at the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">2003 Rugby World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 Rugby League World Cup</a> and concerts, including the <a href="/wiki/U2_360%C2%B0_Tour" title="U2 360° Tour">U2 360° Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Brisbane_Roar_season" title="2010–11 Brisbane Roar season">2010–11 Season</a>, during negotiations with the operator of Suncorp Stadium, there were suggestions that the club may move its home games to <a href="/wiki/Ballymore_Stadium" title="Ballymore Stadium">Ballymore Stadium</a> where the club has its administration and training facilities. However, the owners of the club opted to stay at Suncorp Stadium on a new restructured contract that would ensure the financial viability of hosting games at the more expensive Suncorp Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the flooding of Suncorp Stadium in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Queensland_floods" title="2010–2011 Queensland floods">2010–2011 Queensland floods</a>, the Roar were forced to move two home games against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wellington_Phoenix" title="Wellington Phoenix">Wellington Phoenix</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melbourne_Heart" title="Melbourne Heart">Melbourne Heart</a> to the regular home of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_United" title="Gold Coast United">Gold Coast United</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skilled_Park" title="Skilled Park">Skilled Park</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>. These matches are the first 'home' league fixtures that the Roar have played at a venue other than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suncorp_Stadium" title="Suncorp Stadium">Suncorp Stadium</a> in the club's history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foxsports.com.au_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-foxsports.com.au-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a spectacular <a href="/wiki/2011_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2011 A-League Grand Final">2011 A-League Grand Final</a>, the 50,168 strong fans would make history, being the largest crowd to watch both the Roar and a football match in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>. This was bettered the following season when 50,334 people saw Brisbane defeat Perth in the <a href="/wiki/2012_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2012 A-League Grand Final">2012 A-League Grand Final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-32">[32]</a></sup> The attendance of the 2012 Grand Final would be bettered two years later when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013-14_A-League" title="2013-14 A-League">2013–14 Premiers</a>, the Roar, would do the double, beating <span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Western Sydney Wanderers !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Western_Sydney_Wanderers_FC" title="Western Sydney Wanderers FC">Western Sydney Wanderers</a></span> in the <a href="/wiki/2014_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2014 A-League Grand Final">2014 A-League Grand Final</a> in front of 51,153 passionate sets of fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>During their 2015–16 campaign, the Nathan campus of <a href="/wiki/Griffith_University" title="Griffith University">Griffith University</a> became Brisbane Roar's new training base, with the Roar’s contract at long-time training venue <a href="/wiki/Ballymore_Stadium" title="Ballymore Stadium">Ballymore Stadium</a> expiring, and the field at their previous <a href="/wiki/Perry_Park,_Brisbane" title="Perry Park, Brisbane">Perry Park</a> administration base not meeting the standards required by the Roar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Later, in 2016, Brisbane announced the club would move to a permanent administration and training facility in <a href="/wiki/Logan_City" title="Logan City">Logan City</a>. The $9 million Logan Metro Sports Park will also be the home to the club's academy, youth and women's sides, as well as <a href="/wiki/Football_Brisbane" title="Football Brisbane">Football Brisbane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Prior to the commencement of the 2016–17, it was announced that Brisbane would return to Ballymore for at least another year, due to the club's new Logan training fields not being complete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliations">Affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Affiliations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia"><img alt="Australia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="1280" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queensland_Lions_Soccer_Club" title="Queensland Lions Soccer Club">Queensland Lions</a> – Founded the club and played a part in Queensland Roar's inaugural roster.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership_and_finances">Ownership and finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ownership and finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Currently, the club is owned by:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aburizal_Bakrie" title="Aburizal Bakrie">The Bakrie Group</a> – 100%</li>
</ul>
<p>Brisbane Roar was established by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queensland_Lions_SC" title="Queensland Lions SC">Queensland Lions SC</a> in March 2005 as the team that would represent Brisbane in the newly formed <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>. Queensland Lions held a majority share in the club through to 2008. It is understood that in 2008 the 25% share owned by Queensland Lions was bought by the Roar board at a discount. This led to financial instability in the club and rumours of the club handing back its A-League licence to <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia" title="Football Federation Australia">Football Federation Australia (FFA)</a>. On 16 April 2009 reports surfaced that the FFA were willing to purchase up to a 55% share in the Roar to ensure its financial stability. This 55% encompassed CEO Lawrence Oudendyk's 15% per cent interest, the 25% previously owned by Queensland Lions and the 15% share owned by Rob Jones and Rob Jansen. FFA advised that any takeover by the FFA would see Oudendyk replaced as CEO.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Ultimately a new Brisbane-based ownership structure was formed with investors Emmanuel Drivas, Emmanuel Kokoris, Claude Baradel and Serge Baradel taking over 100% ownership of the club.</p>
<p>On 30 April 2009 the FFA confirmed their offer to take a controlling share in the Roar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The new ownership group declined the FFA's assistance on 22 May 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The owners' commitment to the club was reinforced in a statement released by Emmanuel Drivas on behalf of the owners on 12 April 2010 after further speculation that the Roar would require financial assistance from the FFA after a poor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar_season_2009%E2%80%9310" title="Brisbane Roar season 2009–10">2009–10 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2011, just a week after the club won its first Grand Final, the FFA would take back the club's licence, agreeing to fund the club until new owners were found. Football Federation Australia CEO <a href="/wiki/Ben_Buckley" title="Ben Buckley">Ben Buckley</a> thanked the previous owners for pouring money into the Roar, who could not keep up with the future costs for the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 October 2011, <a href="/wiki/The_World_Game" title="The World Game">The World Game</a> reported that <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> mining magnate, The Bakrie Group, would takeover ownership of the club from the FFA under a 10-year term. Under the terms of the deal, The Bakrie Group paid A$8 million for a 70% share of the club, with the FFA retaining the remaining 30% share. Under the terms of this deal, the Bakrie Group had the option to purchase a further 20% stake in the club with the FFA holding the remaining 10% share. The Bakrie Group also own <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_Super_League" title="Indonesia Super League">Indonesia Super League</a> club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arema_Cronus_F.C." title="Arema Cronus F.C.">Arema Cronus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division" title="Belgian Second Division">Belgian Second Division</a> club <a href="/wiki/C.S._Vis%C3%A9" title="C.S. Visé">C.S. Visé</a>. Following this change of ownership, the new chairman of the Roar was announced as Dali Tahir.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>After becoming the first majority-share foreign owner of an A-League team, on 6 February 2012, the FFA announced that Bakrie had acquired 100 percent ownership of the Brisbane club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 June, it was reported that the Roar's owners, The Bakrie Group, were 9 billion dollars in debt, after having promising to inject 3.5 million dollars into the club. It was later revealed that players and staff, who were due to paid on 15 June – had yet to be remunerated for the month amid growing concerns over the ongoing viability of the three-time champion under the control of the Bakries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was announced on 10 July 2015, Brisbane Roar owner The Bakrie Group will sell the A-League club and a new owner will own the club later this month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> On 25 July the <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia" title="Football Federation Australia">Football Federation Australia</a> threatened to wind up the Brisbane Roar due to unpaid debts <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p><br/></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:305px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Roar_supporters_(8398837736).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="594" data-file-width="792" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Brisbane_Roar_supporters_%288398837736%29.jpg/303px-Brisbane_Roar_supporters_%288398837736%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Brisbane_Roar_supporters_%288398837736%29.jpg/455px-Brisbane_Roar_supporters_%288398837736%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Brisbane_Roar_supporters_%288398837736%29.jpg/606px-Brisbane_Roar_supporters_%288398837736%29.jpg 2x" width="303"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="960" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg/220px-Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg/330px-Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg/440px-Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brisbane_Roar_Flares_vs_Gold_Coast_United_December_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Brisbane Roar supporters set off flares during a derby against <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_United_FC" title="Gold Coast United FC">Gold Coast United</a> in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Brisbane Roar have two supporter groups, the main supporter group is known as The Den. The Den are located in Bay 332 of the Northern stand of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suncorp_Stadium" title="Suncorp Stadium">Suncorp Stadium</a>, where they have been since the inaugural season of the A-League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brisbane_Roar_Hyundai_A-League_Season_at_Brisbane_City_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brisbane_Roar_Hyundai_A-League_Season_at_Brisbane_City-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, a breakaway supporters group, the River Jay Crew (RJC), were formed. Originally members of the Den, the RJC were located opposite the Den, in Bay 310 of the Southern Stand of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suncorp_Stadium" title="Suncorp Stadium">Suncorp Stadium</a>. While members of the Den the group was known as Brisbane Gentlemen, however broke away to form their own identity. Prior to the commencement of the 2012/2013 season, Brisbane Roar Football club announced to the River Jay Crew that they would no longer have a designated section in the southern end at Suncorp stadium on match days. The Roar however permitted the group to move to the northern end of the stadium if they wished to actively support the club. The reason for actions taken, in the eyes of the club, were deemed to be down to clothing issues, with offensive language and the wearing of <a href="/wiki/Flare" title="Flare">flares.</a> The issue was fought by the members of the RJC to re-gain a place at Suncorp and continue their support for the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FinalOrangeArmy_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FinalOrangeArmy-49">[49]</a></sup> The group, after many negotiations, was awarded another section in the stadium, section 326, the closest bay to the den on the Eastern stand of the stadium. Since moving to the new section of the stadium, the group would change their name to the All River Singers Elite, the core of the group originally members of the Den. The ARSE moved back to bay 332 with the Den at the start of the 2013/14 season, but still partially hung on to their identity.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: M1 Derby and <a href="/wiki/Australian_regional_rivalries#New_South_Wales_vs_Queensland" title="Australian regional rivalries">New South Wales vs Queensland state rivalry</a></div>
<ul>
<li><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_United" title="Gold Coast United">Gold Coast United</a></i> – Now defunct. Known as the M1 Derby, it shared the name of the main highway between the two cities, the <a href="/wiki/Highway_1_(Queensland)" title="Highway 1 (Queensland)">M1</a>. Due to Brisbane's close proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>, Brisbane Roar's geographical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Derby_match" title="Derby match">derby</a> opponent was naturally going to be <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_United_FC" title="Gold Coast United FC">Gold Coast United</a>. The glitzy Coast side only won 1 more game between the two (4 to 3), having won the first 3 games, all in Gold Coast's first season of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-League_2009-10" title="A-League 2009-10">2009–10</a>. They would, however, win only 1 of the 6 other games the two sides would play. The rivalry, however, concluded on 5 April 2012 when <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia" title="Football Federation Australia">Football Federation Australia</a> officially announced the axing of the Gold Coast side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> There was also a rivalry with (now defunct) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Queensland_Fury" title="North Queensland Fury">North Queensland Fury</a> due to both clubs being in the same state although it was widely considered a regular match due to the distance between the two teams. The Fury was axed just a year prior to Gold Coast United being culled.</li>
<li><b><span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Sydney FC !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a></span></b>  – As the Roar were originally the only A-League team from Queensland and in keeping with the long-standing rivalry between New South Wales and Queensland, specifically for Queensland and all things Sydney-centric, the Roar developed a natural rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a>. This was initially evident by the increased interest reflected in attendances at home games against Sydney FC. The first evidence of this rivalry on a football pitch was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-League_2007-08#Finals_series" title="A-League 2007-08">2007–08 A-League Finals Series</a> when Brisbane Roar (then known as Queensland Roar) secured victory over Sydney FC after two hard fought legs with the second leg being played in front of a then club record crowd of 36,211 at Suncorp Stadium. After being fairly tame on the pitch for the following seasons, the rivalry between the biggest clubs in their respective states re-ignited after Sydney FC ended the Brisbane Roar's record-breaking 36-game unbeaten streak in the A-League on 4 December 2011. The return clash in Brisbane saw an on field confrontation between Sydney's <a href="/wiki/Pascal_Bosschaart" title="Pascal Bosschaart">Pascal Bosschaart</a> and Brisbane's <a href="/wiki/Besart_Berisha" title="Besart Berisha">Besart Berisha</a> following Brisbane Roar's late 2–1 victory at Suncorp Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brisbane_Roar_FC_records_and_statistics#Honours" title="List of Brisbane Roar FC records and statistics">List of Brisbane Roar FC honours</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brisbane_Roar_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Brisbane_Roar_FC_records_and_statistics" title="List of Brisbane Roar FC records and statistics">List of Brisbane Roar FC records and statistics</a>.</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Matt_McKay" title="Matt McKay">Matt McKay</a> presently holds the team record for number of total games played with 196 matches. <a href="/wiki/Besart_Berisha" title="Besart Berisha">Besart Berisha</a> is the all-time highest goalscorer in all competitions for the club with 50 goals (48 in A-League and 2 in ACL). Brisbane Roar's highest league home game attendance was 32,371 in 2007 against <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a>. The highest grand final match hosted by the club was 51,153.</p>
<p>Brisbane Roar currently hold the record for most A-League Championships won, and furthermore hold the greatest unbeaten streak in Australian sport of 36 games undefeated, spanning two seasons. The record considers only the leagues which currently represent the top level in each of the four major football codes, and any predecessors to those leagues. The record does not include other leagues in these sports, including those which were once considered to be of equivalent standard to today's top leagues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
